# Book 1 outline

<!-- This normalized file is generated from the raw DOCX for review/search. Do not treat Markdown heading levels as editorial decisions. -->

<!-- paragraph:1 para_id:00000001 style:Title -->
# Easy tasks for a short break

<!-- paragraph:2 para_id:00000002 style:Normal -->
Bring laptop downstairs to work if upstairs is too distracting

<!-- paragraph:3 para_id:00000003 style:Normal -->
---

<!-- paragraph:4 para_id:00000004 style:Normal -->
Go through the notes for an upcoming scene and consolidate / reformat them

<!-- paragraph:5 para_id:00000005 style:Normal -->
Talk with Chat about worldbuilding

<!-- paragraph:6 para_id:00000006 style:Normal -->
Go through prior chapter notes and pull things that didn’t get covered

<!-- paragraph:7 para_id:00000007 style:Normal -->
Outline future chapters or put events in order

<!-- paragraph:8 para_id:00000008 style:Normal -->
Determine interstitial events between planned scenes and put them in the outline

<!-- paragraph:9 para_id:00000009 style:Normal -->
Write dialogue

<!-- paragraph:11 para_id:0000000B style:Normal -->
Don’t spend too much time on internal dialogue. But, when the characters are processing the environment and problem solving that’s interesting.

<!-- paragraph:12 para_id:0000000C style:Normal -->
Probably better to write in chunks that can be dropped in or out in terms of editing, adding stuff, etc

<!-- paragraph:13 para_id:0000000D style:Normal -->
What am I specifically good at? Therapy, psychology, science, philosophy… mandarin, ASL. Lean into those things

<!-- paragraph:14 para_id:0000000E style:Normal -->
Put on daily to-do list: one specific thing for book per day. Figure it out in the morning, do it some during during the day, can do more if want. (Integrate bullet notes, outline part of chapter, etc).

<!-- paragraph:15 para_id:0000000F style:Normal -->
It’s okay to have people spend a while talking about a mystery

<!-- paragraph:16 para_id:00000010 style:Normal -->
The job of the first (or second… or third) draft isn’t to be “good”, it’s to exist enough to hang the story on so it can become better. There’s already so much more depth and texture to the story because of just writing it out

<!-- paragraph:17 para_id:00000011 style:Normal -->
Stories are about asking questions, not giving answers. Delineate the problems (it feels like the creator is gone, reality is broken, etc) and have the characters work inside them, coming up with ways to deal with what’s happening - but don’t give explicit “answers” like - HOW to think, what actually is going on with the Creator etc - because the answers don’t actually matter

<!-- paragraph:18 para_id:00000012 style:Normal -->
It’s okay to leave in things that aren’t great, as an exposure…

Don’t worry too much about making all the scenes consistent. You’ll probably have to finish the draft before you know the whole plot arc and what you want doing what.

<!-- paragraph:19 para_id:00000013 style:Normal -->
Don’t worry about the project as a whole. Just do your best on each thing.

<!-- paragraph:20 para_id:00000014 style:Normal -->
DO NOT go back and edit scenes. You will have to re-edit them all the next time through anyway.

<!-- paragraph:21 para_id:00000015 style:Normal -->
Having “will they won’t they” moments that end up being something else is good

<!-- paragraph:22 para_id:00000016 style:Title -->
# Things to do when the first draft is done

<!-- paragraph:23 para_id:00000017 style:Normal -->
Things to do once the first draft is done

<!-- paragraph:24 para_id:00000018 style:Normal -->
After book done - do a read thru and outline each chapter as it’s being read (editing notes on bottom - tab by tab). Get the whole thing outlined along with all the themes, motifs etc. etc make a page for each theme like “threads” and how it evolves thru the story.

<!-- paragraph:25 para_id:00000019 style:Normal -->
When making the “skeleton” of the next draft, if there’s a section that’s good / want to keep - highlight or mark it in some way. Then just tag it [section 13] or whatever and put the summary of what happens above and below, like in an outline.

<!-- paragraph:26 para_id:0000001A style:Normal -->
Key elements (per chapter) in the readthru outline - like a one / two sentence summary of the main goals of the chapter

<!-- paragraph:27 para_id:0000001B style:Normal -->
Relevant worldbuilding notes at the bottom of each chapter outline (or separate tab)

<!-- paragraph:28 para_id:0000001C style:Title -->
# Ch37

<!-- paragraph:29 para_id:0000001D style:Normal -->
Maya

<!-- paragraph:31 para_id:0000001F style:Normal -->
Dining - tanelle is definitely still there, they would have had to drag her away screaming

<!-- paragraph:32 para_id:00000020 style:Normal -->
Tense nighttime sexually charged scene - “The Skein is full of paths we’d never expect unless our eyes have been opened to them. I was blind.”

<!-- paragraph:34 para_id:00000022 style:Normal -->
Outline

<!-- paragraph:36 para_id:00000024 style:Normal -->
Aldira is still collecting information but they’re losing a lot of informants and the price is going up. It’s been a hexday and it’s been suspiciously quiet, and Davian keeps getting antsier, wanting to charge off after Archeon, and Maya saying they don’t even know if that’s where his parents actually are.

<!-- paragraph:37 para_id:00000025 style:Normal -->
Maya spends her days training Davian and Selwin and her nights working on her own schema, rewriting the zan lattices to try to at least bring visitor identification online at the gateways, but the ancient system is cumbersome and assumed a near-infinite power input - it’s not efficient. faster and close-range to deal with Archeon, despite Erynn’s insistence that she’s not the Creator, she’s a teenager and she needs to sleep.

<!-- paragraph:38 para_id:00000026 style:Normal -->
He asks her for answers - she talks about how she doesn’t have them, and he’s in the big leagues now.

<!-- paragraph:39 para_id:00000027 style:Normal -->
- Maya has her own training to do. She needs to make faster, close-range schema to deal with Archeon and drill them. She has to do this herself.

<!-- paragraph:40 para_id:00000028 style:Normal -->
- Training together “you’re thinking about too many things at once.” Turn this into a romance scene. “It’s not about being able to perform well in perfect conditions, it’s being able to turn a bad situation into a good one. “ “Davian thinking about what he can give to Maya is just his ability to kill people, or his willingness to do it for her… “

<!-- paragraph:42 para_id:0000002A style:Normal -->
Harvick - if only I’d known all I needed to say was “you can do this”

<!-- paragraph:43 para_id:0000002B style:Normal -->
Ch37 - open from Maya’s perspective. She had thought that when she became a magus she would be joining a group of people who had things figured out. Who knew what their magic did, and why, and had a plan for how to achieve their goals. Instead she realized that the number one among all of them was a broken man hanging onto scraps with powers that he barely understood. No one knew what they were doing, and it seemed that she knew just as much as the rest of them despite her inexperience. -she has the fantasy that one day Niall will wake up and tell her that everything will be all right now, that he was testing her and here are all the answers. But that’s a child’s dream - the way Selwin looks to her now. But there’s some comfort in being a child while you can, so she smiles and projects that image to him and everyone else that the Rezins rule over - I’m here, I do have the answers and the power and I will make things right. She wishes that she had someone else that she could look to like that.

<!-- paragraph:44 para_id:0000002C style:Normal -->
Maya and Davian can talk about how once you step across the threshold to be a magus you can’t go back. Now he’s one of the ones that will have to reassure the others. That’s isolating but it also brings them together. The Shroud has been pulled back from their eyes.

<!-- paragraph:45 para_id:0000002D style:Normal -->
Maya is mad at Harvick or the system for hiding yet another secret from her, or taking it as a comment on her utility and competence

<!-- paragraph:46 para_id:0000002E style:Normal -->
For now, next chapter can abstract a few days passing and she notices he’s proficient and can actually do stuff. She should be frustrated with him but not like mad until he tries to apologize right before they go off to murdertown “you’re in the big leagues now, it’s not like fighting low clades”

<!-- paragraph:47 para_id:0000002F style:Normal -->
Maya get sleep deprived from trying to stay up to compensate for Niall and kinda passes out. Davian sits outside of her room the whole time, making the guards very uncomfortable (he was motivated to bend the bars of his cell)

<!-- paragraph:48 para_id:00000030 style:Normal -->
Maya seeing Davian training and getting hit over and over, need to emphasize the effort and repetition required to go from generally skilled/competent to able to do a specific thing well enough to win.
- It reminds her of herself being trained intensely by Niall when she was young

<!-- paragraph:49 para_id:00000031 style:Normal -->
Callback to martial arts - Maya can dress this up as improving bodily awareness and also working on her own schema, and helping Davian work on his - but it can be horny. Also important for end of book fight.

<!-- paragraph:50 para_id:00000032 style:Normal -->
Maya noticing he’s getting distracted. This is an important link - you can use your mind to very intentionally do magic. But you can also let the unconscious get out of hand and drive the boat. That will be messy and inefficient, and it will seem like it doesn’t make sense. If you can bring phantasy into conscious thought, it will make your actions more in line with your true values

<!-- paragraph:51 para_id:00000033 style:Normal -->
Make Davian’s connection with the Ink more psychotic - like the “it’s there for me to take - I need to take it” or he can tell there’s no choice, everything is conspiring together to push him forwards, or something like that. And then he needs to learn to distance himself from those thoughts, because there’s always an option no matter how many things are stacked against you (whether or not they are)

<!-- paragraph:52 para_id:00000034 style:Normal -->
Is all that thinking (ruminating) doing you any good? Or could you just realize you’re going in circles and let it go. I’m not telling you not to solve problems, I’m just disagreeing that what you’re doing brings you any closer.

<!-- paragraph:54 para_id:00000036 style:Normal -->
So a complete psychopath who accepts what they’re doing can be powerful?

<!-- paragraph:55 para_id:00000037 style:Normal -->
Sure but there are reasons to be a good person other than power

<!-- paragraph:56 para_id:00000038 style:Normal -->
Can we tie in any psychological development with Davian and Maya’s improvement? Pick one thing like flexibility and tie it together? They need to be able to accept each other’s histories, Maya needs to let go of perfectionism and rigidity, and Davian needs to accept that the world is the way it is (which is similar). With questions not answers lol. -this could be something for them to talk about in a vulnerable moment, like at night, and then callback in the final conflicts (where everything seems to be going well and then Niall is hamstrung by his rigidity)

<!-- paragraph:57 para_id:00000039 style:Normal -->
“You’re not the creator, maya - you’re a teenager. Go to sleep!” -he looks at this scared girl using magic and projects an emotionless tyrant onto her

<!-- paragraph:58 para_id:0000003A style:Normal -->
“Does that hurt?” “Only when I move at all.”

<!-- paragraph:60 para_id:0000003C style:Normal -->
Davian and Maya run into each other at night
Melissa thought they’d run into each other in that original tense scene with the Codex, so I should duplicate it but make it actually happen

<!-- paragraph:61 para_id:0000003D style:Normal -->
Maya accuses Davian of getting her to like him so he could rob them better.

<!-- paragraph:62 para_id:0000003E style:Normal -->
Remember that picture of miles and Gwen sitting upside down in spider man. That kind of cute vulnerability and connection between two powerful people who are otherwise isolated is great.

<!-- paragraph:63 para_id:0000003F style:Normal -->
Maya and Davian talking about Niall / Kelyra

<!-- paragraph:64 para_id:00000040 style:Normal -->
Parents are both good and bad and they have to be accepted as a whole. There isn’t a need to integrate everything and say “overall good” or “overall bad.” Everyone has parents and they all do a bunch of shit wrong and a bunch of shit right. Take the good parts and throw away the bad. See them as whole people instead of whatever aspect is the strongest as the moment you’re thinking. -parents are all children too - that’s how it works. It sounds like Niall and Kelyra are both carrying the shadows of their own parents -being forged in the fires of overly aggressive and punitive parenting isn’t “good” but it is itself something to be proud of - that you got through it. Getting through the Rezin or Archeon training at all and using the good parts and rejecting the bad…

<!-- paragraph:65 para_id:00000041 style:Normal -->
Extended downtime

<!-- paragraph:66 para_id:00000042 style:Normal -->
They don’t really have the info to act on yet, til the enemies visit. That gives some extended downtime to give Davian and Maya some more normal interactions

<!-- paragraph:67 para_id:00000043 style:Normal -->
When Davian comes back to the place after his family gets familynapped that time can be extended to give more normal interactions and hand to hand time

<!-- paragraph:68 para_id:00000044 style:Normal -->
⁃	Melissa also would like him to see her being “normal” earlier in the book maybe with Erynn or something and find her more attractive

<!-- paragraph:69 para_id:00000045 style:Normal -->
They see that terror of the void in each other, which lets them realize they have someone else to fight it with. He sees her terror of inadequacy and she sees his guilt and fear of impotence

<!-- paragraph:70 para_id:00000046 style:Normal -->
People say - worry about things only if you can do something about them, and then stop. But the problem is you can ALWAYS do something, and this problem is compounded if you’re a particularly powerful magus. Maya and Davian come from this at different directions - if you can always do something, then you always have some ability to start digging yourself out of a hole of depression. But, if you can always do something then how can you tell when enough is enough? (Questions not answers)

<!-- paragraph:71 para_id:00000047 style:Normal -->
It’s important that Maya is the only one who can’t put her shroud down even when she’s asleep. This plays into it being a subconscious reflex. Niall always taught her she can never let her visage as a magus down (or be vulnerable in any way) and having that from a young age plus her magical potential resulted in a permanent shroud that she can only modulate the intensity and size of. Of course, she gets a lot of kudos for that because it keeps her very “safe”. That also means when she’s feeling threatened or defensive even emotionally the shroud flares, which plays out in some prior scenes. Later on Davian might comment about their opposite issues (he doesn’t have the ability to bring up the full shroud reflexively and she can’t turn hers off) and she might ask if he really thinks it’s a good thing (or someone else comments that).

<!-- paragraph:72 para_id:00000048 style:Normal -->
Maya doesn’t say she wants to be with Davian when she flies away (we already established that edit). She should be kind of over-compensating and untruthful but still finding him alluring. But also she can remind herself she did let her guard down for a second and it confirmed to her that it’s risky to do that, and it’s literally the same guy.

<!-- paragraph:74 para_id:0000004A style:Title -->
# Upcoming scenes

<!-- paragraph:75 para_id:0000004B style:Normal -->
Just get the first draft done! Think how good it will feel! You can rewrite every single chapter and conversation after that if you want!

<!-- paragraph:76 para_id:0000004C style:Normal -->
Remember to project yourself onto Maya as well as Davian - if anything she is in a more similar situation to you

<!-- paragraph:93 para_id:0000005D style:Normal -->
Other people see Maya and Davian argue
What if Tanelle has a hobby where does stuff with zan - chewing her unnamed root (she doesn’t know the name, she just buys it from a guy who doesn’t speak her language).

<!-- paragraph:94 para_id:0000005E style:Normal -->
People need to see their interactions and realize they are into each other even though they are arguing a lot. There are lots of characters for this - zanwrights, Erin, etc although some would be a repeat.

<!-- paragraph:100 para_id:00000064 style:Normal -->
The thing Archeon is missing
The reason Archeon hasn’t drilled martial arts enough is they bought into the “we need high Clade magic” or that magic is all that matters lie. Serathis even knows this too but her focus on improving magical ability has been read myopically by her children.

<!-- paragraph:101 para_id:00000065 style:Normal -->
Archeon’s plan seems really complicated. - of course it is. This is something that undermines the entire high Clade system. If it was easy to figure out, things wouldn’t be the way they are. And, most high Clades even if they did figure it out would want to keep it a secret and use it in their own programs. We don’t know for sure that some low and high Clades right now aren’t hiding the true nature of their abilities behind similar subterfuge.

<!-- paragraph:102 para_id:00000066 style:Normal -->
What if the fertility rate among magi tends to be pretty low (and concealed if high to prevent people from knowing # of unpresented or dead children) but they also live a long time? Something about a Shroud makes you live longer (this could be tied to issues with reality)

<!-- paragraph:103 para_id:00000067 style:Normal -->
I like really old and unknowable beings. Perhaps Elric was one and Serathis is another… Niall powerful youth in comparison

<!-- paragraph:104 para_id:00000068 style:Normal -->
The Drakhals and Archeon visit to make a deal

<!-- paragraph:105 para_id:00000069 style:Normal -->
The Drakhals WANT total collapse, and then a controlled rebuilding with them on top (or at least, that’s an all right backup plan in their books) - in the Rezin citadel.

<!-- paragraph:106 para_id:0000006A style:Normal -->
Drakhal deal - Caius marries Maya and Niall is banished

what if the drakhals accuse Niall of kidnapping one of their children they have rights to from a breeding contract? After Maya saves Davian. Wheels within wheels

<!-- paragraph:108 para_id:0000006C style:Normal -->
“I don’t need to beat you or kill you… I just need to let everyone else know you’re not as strong as you pretend you are.”

<!-- paragraph:109 para_id:0000006D style:Normal -->
⁃	Evand AND Caius and Archeon all visit. Archeon has already replaced her grandson with someone un-presented. They don’t care about the old order - it can all be torn down and they’ll make something new from the ashes.

<!-- paragraph:110 para_id:0000006E style:Normal -->
⁃	After the heart is stolen

<!-- paragraph:112 para_id:00000070 style:Normal -->
⁃	after the Drakhals come to the Rezins after the heart is stolen, Niall pretends to be considering their offer - Maya marrying Caius and then a peaceful handover of the citadel. As soon as they leave he grabs everyone to start planning and they’re like wait what are we doing. He’s like - I am going to kill all of them and end this. That’s what I - what we - do.

<!-- paragraph:113 para_id:00000071 style:Normal -->
⁃	Then they raid the Drakhals.

<!-- paragraph:115 para_id:00000073 style:Normal -->
Marrying the daughter is a way to claim the legacy

<!-- paragraph:116 para_id:00000074 style:Normal -->
It’s important to emphasize how afraid of Niall everyone is. Even when the Heart is stolen they wait to see what happens before they come, wondering if it’s a fluke of some kind. When they do come, they come with overwhelming force hoping to provoke Niall (again) into an unwinnable battle. They think surely either the fight with numerous high Clade magi (Archeon, Drakhal, Lyranth, maybe a “neutral” fourth clade) or an underground fight against empowered Vorren + Archeon (to draw Maya off) will both let them take Niall down AND give them legitimacy (he attacked us in front of witnesses / he mysteriously disappears). -“all that flashy lighting, that ruthlessness… that’s not power - it’s inefficiency and lack of control.” At the same time Niall is terrified of being exposed as weak, but he eventually is baited into going after Vorren. (This is Elric’s plan - to bait Niall into going after Vorren so he dies near the heart. The same reason he wanted Davian to kill him while holding the heart, and both times with Maya there to resurrect him and ensure maximum damage to reality. The only reason the backup plan doesn’t completely destroy reality is that Elric doesn’t physically possess the heart when he kills Davian.)

<!-- paragraph:117 para_id:00000075 style:Normal -->
They tell Davian to hide when Drakhal comes. He attacks Caius when he is saying he wants to marry Maya. Niall ends up pretending to smooth everything over but then immediately when they leave saying we will hit them when they’re separate. Send forerunners after them?

<!-- paragraph:118 para_id:00000076 style:Normal -->
Harvick remembering Elric
- Harvick also has a Codex, from his closer relationship with Elric. And after he finds out that Elric put his aura into these (maybe) he is more obsessed with it

- How it got to be the way it is, why Niall will never accept second place or something
Harvick - I remember the day it all changed. I fantasized about the glitter of blades in a war like the the starry host of heaven. (If he’s in his 60s then that would have been 40 years ago? Two generations. Elric was about 25+ years older than him.) Of course we all knew magi were a thing but they were still people, you could wear them down and kill them. That day when Elric was at the head of our army, I was 16 - but I was big for my age, and I’d lied to join up. And then he told us he didn’t need us, and he walked out in front on his own. Magi used to wear armor you know, they’d done it for hundreds of years because you never know when something will shake your shroud and a stray arrow could pick you off. He was the first one I saw walk out into the field dressed like he was heading to a meeting of scholars. Now I heard his mother had seven husbands before she had him, and she was getting up towards where she wasn’t going to be able to have any more children. Not that there are records of any of this stuff, but I think that she was the rule, not the exception. Anyway, when I saw him bring down lightning on the other army, I and everyone else knew that the days of “glorious” clashes between two huge hosts of men was over. And maybe it was just me, but he looked almost like a god to me then - like he was beyond anything a human could ever aspire to be. I told myself then I would do anything to be by his side. And I did. But something about that power and genius… I tell myself we were close, but he never told me what he was really thinking or why he did what he did…

<!-- paragraph:119 para_id:00000077 style:Normal -->
Pre-raid argument
They need to be in a big fight before the climax of the book, where all their insecurities get aired after Davian tries to make some kind of confession

<!-- paragraph:120 para_id:00000078 style:Normal -->
“You like the things about me that make others not like me, and you want me to make myself better”

<!-- paragraph:122 para_id:0000007A style:Normal -->
Niall and Maya and Davian preparing to attack the Harbingers/Drakhal
Niall - I wanted to see you as a tool because otherwise it hurts too much. But you’re not a tool.

<!-- paragraph:123 para_id:0000007B style:Normal -->
Niall frames his decision to attack Archeon as finally trusting Maya to have his back “let them know we’re here.” Schema for backlash, dissipation, anchoring - accumulation. Layered on each other over and over at the speed of thought. -he frames his decision not to use troops as altruistic even though it puts them at a disadvantage but the real reason is he wants to prove to himself he can still do it. “We are high Clade magi. We don’t need anyone else to be effective. We’re not going to hide behind wasteful tricks.” -his eyes were too intense, desperate

<!-- paragraph:124 para_id:0000007C style:Normal -->
Politically Niall pitches attacking Archeon as making an example that will continue their authority. Maya sees the problems but wants to be trusted. The book can end with some kind of issue with all the high clades being against the Rezins - but what does Kelyra do? Does she show up? The high clades summon all their low clades in force which hasn’t happened since before Niall took over

<!-- paragraph:125 para_id:0000007D style:Normal -->
Their war chariots are designed to not flip or whatever if the horses get blown up

<!-- paragraph:126 para_id:0000007E style:Normal -->
As inner chaos recedes (not by being squashed - holding things down requires energy) then magic becomes stronger. So show distractions and poorly integrated selves getting in the way

<!-- paragraph:128 para_id:00000080 style:Normal -->
Subversion demands much more cognitive load because it’s countering what the other person is doing - essentially you have to be thinking one step ahead

<!-- paragraph:129 para_id:00000081 style:Normal -->
⁃	getting “muscle memory” for common channel configurations would be key

<!-- paragraph:131 para_id:00000083 style:Normal -->
Facing the things you fear is how you overcome your trauma

<!-- paragraph:133 para_id:00000085 style:Normal -->
The catacombs I introduced at the beginning can be where the Drakhals connect to the Harbingers. Vorren has been living down there like the head of his own little clade

<!-- paragraph:134 para_id:00000086 style:Normal -->
Harvick’s friends can volunteer to be scouts for Niall and Maya in the raid - you have disposable scouts that prevent you from getting jumped. Maya wants to stop that but they’re like, it’s your job to help make our dreams reality. Also send my kids a lot of money if I die. -they really are like Harvick huh

<!-- paragraph:135 para_id:00000087 style:Normal -->
It’s totally fine for Harvick to give Davian the sword since he can’t really make himself come (killing another magus or watching Niall die). But, antithesis isn’t what Davian has been training to use, so it could be good for him to use an actual sword. Kelyra gets the double knives which are basically made “for” her by Serathis

<!-- paragraph:136 para_id:00000088 style:Normal -->
A scene where Davian is trying to do some technical tricky thing to stop the wards on a door and Maya just blows it up

<!-- paragraph:137 para_id:00000089 style:Normal -->
Going to attack Archeon
Walking to attack Archeon thru the slums. Maya realizes she’s been working on all this high level arcane stuff but a lot of people can barely look up from the ground to think about survival. Niall says that’s the natural order, the magi above and everyone else below.

<!-- paragraph:138 para_id:0000008A style:Normal -->
The areas far from the spoke roads are where the boundaries between city wedges are, and also are the most poorly maintained and supported. Don’t forget ostensibly Niall and Maya are running the whole city too, through proxies - may need to add a proxy council of low clades that reports to them. That is how they’re all run - low Clade councils reporting to the high Clade

<!-- paragraph:139 para_id:0000008B style:Normal -->
See “endgame matchups” under Lore for scene notes about who fights who (there are multiple tabs, some with very detailed noted)

<!-- paragraph:140 para_id:0000008C style:Normal -->
Saving Kelyra
Kelyra is forced to channel a certain type of subversion (the type for negation or diffusion?) into weapons. It’s all to kill Niall and Maya ostensibly so who knows how she feels about that. -that allows setup of a couple things: first, Serathis noting that her level of Subversion ability is very high. She curses whoever was in charge (herself?) for being too narrow minded in what they were looking for. Second, it shows that Kelyra has her own power that could be used to upend the Clades

<!-- paragraph:141 para_id:0000008D style:Normal -->
Magno-kukri flies in hilt first, so it’s grabbed in an underhand grip, letting it almost be redirected with a “punch” that grabs it and holding the sharp edge away from the arm

<!-- paragraph:142 para_id:0000008E style:Normal -->
Raid - Niall and Maya attack the Drakhals above ground while Davian and Harvick go in under the ground

<!-- paragraph:143 para_id:0000008F style:Normal -->
Can Kelyra die from activating her ink boon / subversion too much to help kill Archeon? Or at least she’s seriously injured to put her out of commission til the next book, or unable to be the leader of the masked clades (can still call them veiled even if they wear masks)

<!-- paragraph:145 para_id:00000091 style:Normal -->
Kelyra’s strength is that speed of mind. Because Archeon is combining two types of magic (and martial arts) it’s extra hard to hold it all together. Serathis is constantly frustrated at her children being so “stupid” that they have to learn predictable attack patterns. Kelyra never manifested a Shroud because she is more on the mind-speed/subversion end of the spectrum - not inheriting enough of that Shroud bloodline. But somehow, Davian did - or his mind has been altered by the Ink enough - to have a Shroud while retaining Kelyra’s strengths. -it’s like using a sword in each hand… and one in your foot. You can’t actually do it unless most of the actions are unconscious and can be autonomous for long enough (like running, or jumping) that focus-switching can manage them before they break down

Elric kills Davian
Just to make it more explicit. Elric manipulates everyone and everything through his ability to see and nudge the “dark threads” the represent actions that are aligned with trauma and urges rather than core beliefs. And he has plans within plans with backup plans, all of which the characters are helpless against due to not even knowing he’s there (or being able to mentalize their own issues). He represents the ultimate “invisible conductor” that causes people to feel like their actions are out of their control and they’re just passive observers.

<!-- paragraph:243 para_id:000000F3 style:Normal -->
The ink boons represent Elric tipping the scales a bit - he can see the future if everyone behaves toxically but he also isn’t above tipping the scales to ensure an outcome he wants. Even with tipping the scales he didn’t anticipate Davian working with Maya and Niall, him giving up the ability to kill Vorren himself, and Niall recovering enough to participate, and Maya giving up control enough to rely on both of them. That should be pretty disconcerting how far out of his sight things went. But that’s why he has backup plan upon backup plan and leans heavily on the scales.

Shiva - it’s hard for Westerners to understand, but to obtain perfection, all existing things must be annihilated, no matter how pretty or nice or meaningful they seem

<!-- paragraph:249 para_id:000000F9 style:Normal -->
It’s important for both the characters and the readers to feel like the actions that happen are inevitable, that the tide of trauma is too much. Elric seemingly being behind everything and knowing what’s going to happen is relevant to that - his seeming omnipotence and omniscience emphasize the power of trauma and learned scripts. So it’s also important at the end for him to make reference to how much he had to lean on the scales, and how that’s unexpected, because he is entirely unable to account for the personal growth of the characters, healthy love rather than obsession, Harvick’s drive to help that’s driven by his love for Elric, etc. Harvick is really the biggest fly in the ointment for Elric - who can’t understand the love that Harvick had (has?) for him and the drive that’s provided to nudge and push and pull people off the dark threads.

When Maya uses fateweaving she goes into that space so fast and outside of time even Niall can’t keep up

<!-- paragraph:256 para_id:00000100 style:Normal -->
Shared “fate ties” are a narrative tradition in Buddhist and daoist scenarios. It links to an overarching desire for interdependence that conflicts with western ideas of independence. It’s actually impossible to be perfectly independent so the fate ties work well with the story of Maya and Davian trying to do things on their own and failing.

<!-- paragraph:310 para_id:00000136 style:Normal -->
Conclusion stuff

<!-- paragraph:311 para_id:00000137 style:Normal -->
End of book - Elric, fully re-crystallized, within the young body & with powers similar to Niall’s

<!-- paragraph:312 para_id:00000138 style:Normal -->
To summarize: Elric convinced Serathis he could get her in charge of all the High Clades, to tear the order down. He would have to be even older than her. He convinced Vorren that he wanted Vorren to destroy everything. He convinced Evana he thought political maneuvering could accomplish the world he wanted. He took over the underworld and Masked Clades by playing populist/anarchist. So he played all of them against each other and the Rezins under the guise of wanting a new world, while secretly plotting to destroy reality. <!-- paragraph:327 para_id:00000147 style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:360 para_id:00000168 style:Normal -->
She clung to the thread with clenched mental fingers, forcing her focus along the single dark line that represented Arrek moving through the city. It was like trying to run along a taut wire in a hurricane. Every second, torrents of possibility slammed against her—sideways branches, future-eddies, dying threads that yanked at her like undertow.

<!-- paragraph:361 para_id:00000169 style:Normal -->
She kept going. Follow him. Find him. Fix it.

<!-- paragraph:362 para_id:0000016A style:Normal -->
The thread shuddered suddenly.

<!-- paragraph:363 para_id:0000016B style:Normal -->
Arrek heard something in the alley and turned toward it, his hand closing around the handle of that strange black chisel he carried like a talisman. The moment his fingers touched it—the thread she followed detonated.

<!-- paragraph:364 para_id:0000016C style:Normal -->
Pure fate—not the soft shimmer she wielded but the violent, cataclysmic force she had seen only in visions—burst outward from the blade, slamming her awareness sideways. Her psyche spiraled off the line, flung helplessly into the roaring storm of the Skein.

<!-- paragraph:365 para_id:0000016D style:Normal -->
The world became an ocean in mid-tempest. She tumbled through it—and then a vision snapped into being, sharp enough to hurt.

<!-- paragraph:366 para_id:0000016E style:Normal -->
The chisel—no, a knife, long and black and wrong—spun into the hand of a young woman in a mask as she surged forward, launching herself at the back of a man wearing the sleeveless garb of a High Clade magus. She raised the blade toward his neck—

<!-- paragraph:367 para_id:0000016F style:Normal -->
A Shroud erupted around him. A cataclysmic detonation, omnidirectional, cracking the stone beneath his feet, vaporizing the air in a ring around him. The masked woman slammed into the ground like a rag doll, her body mangled, then going still. Dead.

<!-- paragraph:368 para_id:00000170 style:Normal -->
As the magus turned, Maya saw his face—unfamiliar, ecstatic, eyes wide with the thrill of destruction. And the sigil flaring across his skin—Drakhal.

<!-- paragraph:369 para_id:00000171 style:Normal -->
Her breath caught. Then the Skein seized her and flung her again—another thread, another slice of time, the same man, the same deranged glint in his eyes—Facing off against someone she recognized instantly.

<!-- paragraph:370 para_id:00000172 style:Normal -->
Caius Drakhal. Younger. Paler. Afraid. Caius thrust his hand forward, blasting a wave of force that warped the air—The deranged magus swatted it aside like dust. And then he was on Caius.

<!-- paragraph:371 para_id:00000173 style:Normal -->
An explosion of force flared from his body, blasting outward in all directions, throwing attendants and stone debris across the courtyard. He grabbed Caius by the jaw and slammed his head into the ground—once, twice, again—each impact cracking stone, spraying blood.

<!-- paragraph:372 para_id:00000174 style:Normal -->
Ivana Drakhal appeared at the edge of the scene, her face white. “Vorren, enough!” But the magus didn’t stop. Didn’t even slow down.

<!-- paragraph:373 para_id:00000175 style:Normal -->
Not until Ivana unleashed a focused blast—a compressed beam of force so sharp it distorted the air. It struck the magus in the chest, lifting him from his feet and off Caius - slamming him into a wall with such power it cratered the stone, spiderweb cracks radiating out like a shattering mirror.

<!-- paragraph:374 para_id:00000176 style:Normal -->
The vision trembled—thread snapping—

And Maya felt herself being pulled again, deeper, toward something darker.

## 0) Timeline & frame

## 1) Opening beat — Aftermath stillness; work paused; body count

Davian internal:

<!-- paragraph:487 para_id:000001E7 style:Normal -->
Pain inventory (forearms, ribs), little pride flicker at surviving Brann → immediately drowned by humiliation and defensive rage (his familiar buffer against trauma).

<!-- paragraph:899 para_id:00000383 style:Normal -->
The journey back to the Rezin citadel had been a blur of movement and tension. Maya recalled the streets of Elarion—dim and quiet in the twilight, yet brimming with unspoken judgments. Niall’s urgency had been unmistakable, his silence more telling than words. Even the Ironstriders beneath them had seemed to sense his mood, their steps quicker, their motions sharper.

<!-- paragraph:900 para_id:00000384 style:Normal -->
Through the citadel gates, they had dismounted without ceremony. Niall’s stride had been brisk, his focus unyielding, and Maya had found herself falling into step behind him without question. She hadn’t known what to say, and Niall, for all his intensity, had offered nothing to break the silence. All she could feel was the weight of her own words from the Presentation, reverberating in her mind.

<!-- paragraph:901 para_id:00000385 style:Normal -->
Niall had said nothing as they passed through the citadel’s halls. Instead, he led her directly to the secluded training courtyard. The space was both familiar and comforting, the place where she had honed her magic over countless hours. The polished stone floor bore faint scorch marks and frost-rimed cracks from past sessions, and the shelves lining the walls were stacked with various arcane tools—runes, chisels, and inert glyphs awaiting activation.

<!-- paragraph:902 para_id:00000386 style:Normal -->
He waved off the attendants and stationed guards at the entrance, their expressions stern as they took their posts. The heavy door shut with a finality that made Maya’s heart quicken.

<!-- paragraph:903 para_id:00000387 style:Normal -->
The last rays of sunlight slanted through the high walls of the courtyard, catching the faint glow of glyphs etched into the stone and making the air shimmer with latent energy. Niall turned to face her, his sharp gaze cutting through the silence like a blade.

<!-- paragraph:1072 para_id:00000430 style:Normal -->
Chapter 14

<!-- paragraph:1074 para_id:00000432 style:Normal -->
Davian navigates the slums to meet Jalen, evading potential surveillance and reflecting on his emotionally numbed, routine-driven existence.

<!-- paragraph:1075 para_id:00000433 style:Normal -->
Jalen and Davian communicate in sign, discussing the slow progress of the mission and the looming danger of the Ink Boon’s expiration. Jalen admits unrest in the Concord and the threat of a leadership challenge, but insists on finishing the job to repay their debt to the Syndicate.

<!-- paragraph:1076 para_id:00000434 style:Normal -->
Davian returns to the citadel, frustrated by the disparity between the High Clade’s comfort and the suffering in the slums. A casual, friendly interaction with a gate guard underscores Davian’s inner conflict—he resents the system but finds moments of connection within it.

<!-- paragraph:1077 para_id:00000435 style:Normal -->
Dinner in the mess hall is endured rather than enjoyed; Tanelle’s chatter helps mask Davian’s detachment.

<!-- paragraph:1078 para_id:00000436 style:Normal -->
Harvick brings Davian to a special training courtyard, which turns out to be where Maya is practicing, showcasing her overwhelming magical power.

<!-- paragraph:1079 para_id:00000437 style:Normal -->
Davian is struck by Maya’s presence, beauty, and power, sparking conflicted feelings—rage, attraction, and awe—all filtered through his internal narrative of resistance and resentment.

<!-- paragraph:1080 para_id:00000438 style:Normal -->
Harvick uses the chaos of Maya’s training as a mental training ground, arguing that just as physical discomfort builds strength, mental discomfort sharpens focus. Davian is embarrassed, distracted, and frustrated, but ultimately recommits to pushing through the psychological challenge.

<!-- paragraph:1081 para_id:00000439 style:Normal -->
The chapter shows Davian’s increasing emotional conflict, his unstable sense of self, and the beginnings of Maya becoming a focal point in his internal struggle. It deepens the theme of inner discipline vs emotional suppression.

Chapter 12 outline
Davian struggles to secretly disable the treasury sphere’s glyphs using Subversion, discovering it’s far more difficult than anticipated due to complex redundancies.

<!-- paragraph:1121 para_id:00000461 style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:1122 para_id:00000462 style:Normal -->
Harvick reassures Davian he sees through his act, acknowledges his difficult past, and encourages him to consider joining the guard permanently for protection, sensing he's hiding from something.

<!-- paragraph:1125 para_id:00000465 style:Normal -->
Chapter 11 outline

<!-- paragraph:1127 para_id:00000467 style:Normal -->
Maya’s Reflection on Davian’s Stare: As Maya descends the spiral staircase, she reflects on an unsettling interaction with a contractor (Davian) who stared at her in an intense, almost angry way, unlike anyone else she has encountered.

<!-- paragraph:1128 para_id:00000468 style:Normal -->
Erynn’s Antics: At the base of the stairs, Maya finds Erynn sitting and teasingly suggests she should join her climbs. Erynn jokes that she prefers being "ready and fresh" rather than exhausted and sweaty.

<!-- paragraph:1129 para_id:00000469 style:Normal -->
Maya’s Concern About the Journal: Maya decides to return to her quarters to rest, prompting Erynn to ask if it’s about the journal. Maya dismisses the question but retrieves the journal once alone, reflecting on the vivid and potentially dangerous memories it holds.

<!-- paragraph:1130 para_id:0000046A style:Normal -->
Journal Memory – Her Parents’ First Encounter: Maya accesses a memory where her mother and a young, authoritative magus—later revealed as her father—clash during a parlay. Her mother confronts him with fiery disdain for Elarion’s caste system, and he expresses regret that they’re on opposite sides of the conflict. Maya realizes her parents met during the war.

<!-- paragraph:1131 para_id:0000046B style:Normal -->
Maya’s Unsettling Connection: Back in her room, Maya reflects on how her father’s gaze in the memory reminds her of the nameless contractor’s (Davian) stare, leaving her uneasy.

<!-- paragraph:1132 para_id:0000046C style:Normal -->
Erynn’s Guard Crush: Maya exits her quarters, allowing Erynn to stay outside to flirt with a guard. Later, Maya pulls Erynn away, and they walk down a corridor.

<!-- paragraph:1133 para_id:0000046D style:Normal -->
Maya’s Query About Staring: Maya asks Erynn what it means when a man stares at you, prompting Erynn’s intrigue and playful teasing. Maya evades specifics, saying the question is theoretical, though she internally notes she is thinking of both her father and Davian.

<!-- paragraph:1134 para_id:0000046E style:Normal -->
Alden’s Analysis on Drakhal and the Attack: Maya visits Alden’s office to discuss the citadel attack. Alden explains that the High Clades have already moved on politically and suggests that even proof against Drakhal wouldn’t matter now.

<!-- paragraph:1135 para_id:0000046F style:Normal -->
Darius Drakhal’s Courtship Letter: Alden gives Maya a letter from Darius Drakhal requesting to meet her, likely for courtship. Maya is shocked, while Erynn is ecstatic and gushes about Darius’ handsomeness and the political advantages of the match.

<!-- paragraph:1136 para_id:00000470 style:Normal -->
Maya’s Frustration with Erynn: As they leave, Erynn continues to chatter enthusiastically about Darius, prompting Maya to sharply order her to stop talking. Despite this, Erynn remains amused and intrigued by the situation.

<!-- paragraph:1139 para_id:00000473 style:Normal -->
Chapter 10 outline

Restless Morning: Davian wakes up after a poor night of sleep, skipping breakfast to avoid small talk. He learns that only the supervisors are meeting with Lady Maya in the morning, giving the rest of the workers free time.

<!-- paragraph:1140 para_id:00000474 style:Normal -->
Exploring the Citadel: Davian uses the free time to explore the citadel. He notes the spire’s design as the citadel’s original centerpiece, with walls and outbuildings radiating outward to form a self-contained city. He observes the spire's defensiveness, with no entrances facing the city and only arrow slits for windows until high above.

<!-- paragraph:1141 para_id:00000475 style:Normal -->
Speculating on the Vault: While walking, Davian speculates that the vault is likely higher within the spire for security reasons. Though tempted to scout the interior, he decides against risking attention, trusting that his assignment on the wards will eventually reveal what he needs.

<!-- paragraph:1142 para_id:00000476 style:Normal -->
Preparation for Glyphwright Work: Back in his room, Davian reviews a glyphwright manual to prepare. Though he has a solid foundation from his parents, he worries about working in front of others. He hopes to be paired with someone talkative and distracted, concluding with chagrin that this will likely be Tanelle.

<!-- paragraph:1143 para_id:00000477 style:Normal -->
Meeting Assignments: At the meeting outbuilding, Davian positions himself next to Tanelle, who is thrilled to work with him. They follow Supervisor Marek into the spire, ascending an exhausting spiral staircase. Tanelle talks incessantly, even as the climb leaves her breathless, while Davian notes how the staircase confirms the treasury and vaults are above ground.

<!-- paragraph:1144 para_id:00000478 style:Normal -->
Introduction to the Treasury: At the top of the stairs, the group enters a grand chamber dominated by an enormous floating stone sphere—the treasury. Marek explains that weightlessness in the chamber allows access to the sphere, controlled by the Registry as both a security measure and a potential trap.

<!-- paragraph:1145 para_id:00000479 style:Normal -->
Weightlessness Training: The group is told to acclimate to the chamber’s weightlessness, with Marek warning against reckless jumps without ropes. Davian adapts quickly but must save Tanelle twice from drifting into walls. Using her distraction, he drifts closer to the sphere, observing its intricate carvings and the doorway leading inside. He feels an odd pull, imagining the Heart pulsing faintly within.

<!-- paragraph:1146 para_id:0000047A style:Normal -->
Assignments Begin: Marek calls the group back to the floor and assigns tasks. Davian ensures he’s paired with Tanelle to learn the work by following her lead. She proves surprisingly skilled at glyphwright work, re-etching and replacing sequences with confidence. Her constant chatter about the glyphs helps Davian learn what to do.

<!-- paragraph:1147 para_id:0000047B style:Normal -->
Encounter with Maya: Maya enters the chamber, using jets of flame to float gracefully through the air. Davian observes her, recalling her powerful display on the wall. His pulse quickens, though he insists it’s anger. When Maya’s gaze locks onto him, he realizes he’s been glaring. Flushing, he bows awkwardly and mutters a greeting. By the time he looks up, she is already gone.

<!-- paragraph:1148 para_id:0000047C style:Normal -->
Renewed Focus: Davian watches Maya float away, then steels himself for the tasks ahead. He knows that the challenges of the treasury are just the beginning.

<!-- paragraph:1149 para_id:0000047D style:Normal -->
Plan to drop the treasury on Niall

<!-- paragraph:1151 para_id:0000047F style:Normal -->
Chapter 9 outline

<!-- paragraph:1153 para_id:00000481 style:Normal -->
Reviewing the Proposal:
Maya reviews a detailed work proposal from the new supervisor of the combined contractor group, impressed by its thoroughness despite minor flaws.

<!-- paragraph:1154 para_id:00000482 style:Normal -->
Receiving Decryption Materials:
In her quarters, Maya finds books provided by Alden on decoding auratic codices and retrieves her mother's journal.

<!-- paragraph:1155 para_id:00000483 style:Normal -->
Unlocking the Codex:
Maya discovers an incantation inside the journal and uses it to access a vivid memory, experiencing her mother fighting against Elarion's forces.

<!-- paragraph:1156 para_id:00000484 style:Normal -->
Reflecting on the Memory:
The memory reveals her mother as powerful, purposeful, and ruthless, leaving Maya questioning the pettiness of High Clade politics and her own place within it.

<!-- paragraph:1157 para_id:00000485 style:Normal -->
Conversation with Niall:
At breakfast, Maya asks Niall why her mother came to Elarion. He deflects but eventually admits Maya reminds him of her mother, leaving the conversation unresolved and tense.

<!-- paragraph:1158 para_id:00000486 style:Normal -->
Confiding in Erynn:
Maya tells Erynn about the journal and the memory. Erynn jokingly asks if Maya plans to go rogue, to which Maya responds she is frustrated with High Clade games but uncertain about her next steps.

<!-- paragraph:1159 para_id:00000487 style:Normal -->
Overseeing the Wards Project:
At the meeting with the glyphwright supervisors, Maya outlines plans for overhauling the treasury and vault wards, which integrate with the Registry to identify and neutralize threats with lethal magic.

<!-- paragraph:1160 para_id:00000488 style:Normal -->
Assignment to the Treasury:
Maya assigns Group One to the treasury wards first, explaining the vault wards are significantly more dangerous and require preparation before they can safely proceed.

<!-- paragraph:1161 para_id:00000489 style:Normal -->
Emphasizing Caution:
Maya reminds the supervisors about the risks, hazard pay, and strict protocols, including searches and limited access, to safeguard the citadel's treasures.

<!-- paragraph:1162 para_id:0000048A style:Normal -->
Key Work on Vault Wards:
After dismissing the supervisors, Maya confides in Erynn that she plans to handle the vault’s most dangerous work herself while quietly assessing who is competent enough to assist her

<!-- paragraph:1163 para_id:0000048B style:Normal -->

Davian is relieved when Maya dismisses the contractors and they are allowed to leave the meeting hall after aura verifications.

<!-- paragraph:1167 para_id:0000048F style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:1168 para_id:00000490 style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:1171 para_id:00000493 style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:1173 para_id:00000495 style:Normal -->
Escape to the Courtyard:

<!-- paragraph:1174 para_id:00000496 style:Normal -->
To avoid further attention, Davian hastily finishes his meal and excuses himself to "exercise."

<!-- paragraph:1175 para_id:00000497 style:Normal -->
In the courtyard, he practices a simple hand-to-hand kata his mother taught him to regain focus and control.

<!-- paragraph:1176 para_id:00000498 style:Normal -->
Sparring with Harvick:

<!-- paragraph:1177 para_id:00000499 style:Normal -->
Davian is interrupted by Harvick, a middle-aged Rezin guard, who playfully teases him about his "dancing."

<!-- paragraph:1178 para_id:0000049A style:Normal -->
Harvick insists on sparring, and Davian reluctantly agrees, pretending to be less skilled than he is.

<!-- paragraph:1179 para_id:0000049B style:Normal -->
Frustrated and humiliated when Harvick accuses him of holding back, Davian fights more earnestly, but Harvick ultimately disarms him.

<!-- paragraph:1180 para_id:0000049C style:Normal -->
Harvick introduces himself and offers to spar with Davian again, suspecting there’s more to him than his claim of being a glyphwright.

<!-- paragraph:1181 para_id:0000049D style:Normal -->
Paranoia and Isolation:

<!-- paragraph:1182 para_id:0000049E style:Normal -->
Back in his room, Davian reflects on the day, particularly Maya’s lethal composure and Harvick’s skill.

<!-- paragraph:1183 para_id:0000049F style:Normal -->
Paranoia sets in as he fears Harvick was testing him or that the Rezins might already suspect his true identity.

<!-- paragraph:1184 para_id:000004A0 style:Normal -->
His nerves worsen when Tanelle checks on him, amplifying his fear that she’s spying for the Rezins.

<!-- paragraph:1185 para_id:000004A1 style:Normal -->
Nightmare and Guilt:

<!-- paragraph:1186 para_id:000004A2 style:Normal -->
Unable to rest, Davian eventually falls into a nightmare where he repeatedly kills Arrek, only for the face to shift into his sister Selina’s.

<!-- paragraph:1187 para_id:000004A3 style:Normal -->
He wakes drenched in sweat, consumed by guilt over failing Selina and obsessively repeating that he must "make it right" by killing Niall.

<!-- paragraph:1189 para_id:000004A5 style:Normal -->
Chapter 7 outline

<!-- paragraph:1190 para_id:000004A6 style:Normal -->
Maya’s Reaction to the Assassination Attempt: Maya leaves the meeting hall radiating calm but collapses into a chair in private, struggling with the weight of having killed the assassin. She dissociates briefly but regains her composure when Alden arrives.

<!-- paragraph:1191 para_id:000004A7 style:Normal -->
Investigation Details: Maya demands to know how the attack was possible. Alden reveals the assassin bypassed vetting through a bribe and assumed a dead contractor’s identity. He informs her that the Sorevin family, who managed the contractor records, was wiped out during a coordinated attack to steal their lists. Alden speculates that a High Clade could be orchestrating these assassinations for political purposes but dismisses rumors of "the Shade," a mythical assassin figure.

<!-- paragraph:1192 para_id:000004A8 style:Normal -->
Maya’s Response: Maya decides to return to the meeting hall to maintain her composure and authority, refusing to let the attackers think they’ve unsettled her. Alden confirms the remaining contractors have been verified through the Registry.

<!-- paragraph:1193 para_id:000004A9 style:Normal -->
Returning to the Hall: Maya promotes the Group One supervisor to oversee the team left without leadership and demands an adjusted schedule by day’s end. She notices the assassin’s remains have been removed, likely for Alden’s analysis.

<!-- paragraph:1194 para_id:000004AA style:Normal -->
Maya’s Office: Maya retreats to her luxurious office, described in grand detail, where Erynn arrives, distraught over Maya’s safety. Maya briefly allows herself a moment of vulnerability before resuming her composed demeanor when Niall enters.

<!-- paragraph:1195 para_id:000004AB style:Normal -->
Interaction with Niall: Niall commends Maya’s handling of the attack but pushes her to recount the details, causing her to dissociate. Erynn defends Maya, but Maya insists on continuing. Niall kneels beside her, apologizing for the burdens he places on her, but Maya accuses him of treating her like a problem rather than a daughter. Their conversation is interrupted by Alden.

<!-- paragraph:1196 para_id:000004AC style:Normal -->
Alra’s Betrayal: Alra, the scribe who facilitated the assassin’s entry, is brought in and interrogated. She reveals her betrayal was motivated by grief over her brother, who died protecting Maya during the war. Niall prepares to execute her, but Maya intervenes, deciding to exile Alra instead, stripping her from the Registry. Alra is dragged away, screaming insults at Maya.

<!-- paragraph:1197 para_id:000004AD style:Normal -->
Maya Questions Alden: After the others leave, Maya privately asks Alden how to decrypt an encrypted journal. Alden identifies it as likely a memory journal, requiring a specific incantation to unlock encoded memories. He offers to send her reading materials and warns her about the vivid, potentially overwhelming nature of such journals.

<!-- paragraph:1200 para_id:000004B0 style:Normal -->
Chapter 6 outline

<!-- paragraph:1201 para_id:000004B1 style:Normal -->
Exploration of Arrek’s House:
 Davian and Jalen search Arrek’s cramped, dilapidated home, looking for anything that could expose Davian’s disguise or help him pass as a glyphwright. The house reveals Arrek’s struggles, including a journal detailing his sacrifices to send money to free his cousins from debt contracts. This discovery reminds Davian of Selina and the cruelty of the High Clades.

<!-- paragraph:1202 para_id:000004B2 style:Normal -->
Jalen Transfers the Ink Boon:
 In a heated exchange, Davian accuses Jalen of forcing him to kill Arrek. Jalen reveals his guilt over Selina’s death and his belief that killing Niall Rezin could strike back at the High Clades. He transfers the Ink Boon to Davian, emphasizing the stakes and their shared purpose of making the High Clades feel fear.

<!-- paragraph:1203 para_id:000004B3 style:Normal -->
Preparations for the Mission:
 Through the night, Davian studies glyphwright texts with Jalen’s guidance. Though overwhelmed, he begins to grasp the basics, knowing he must appear competent enough to avoid suspicion but not so skilled as to draw attention.

<!-- paragraph:1204 para_id:000004B4 style:Normal -->
Arrival at the Rezin Citadel:
 Davian parts ways with Jalen and Garren as he approaches the citadel. Using Arrek’s glyphwright contract, he introduces himself as “Arrek Hadrin” to the guards and is processed for entry. He notes the oppressive security measures and the citadel’s overwhelming arcane power.

<!-- paragraph:1205 para_id:000004B5 style:Normal -->
Registry Process:
 Davian is escorted to the Registry, a room where all contractors are magically logged. Under the sharp gaze of the Rezin spymaster, he undergoes the process of inputting his aura and false name. The process is invasive and disquieting, further cementing Davian’s resentment toward the High Clades.

<!-- paragraph:1206 para_id:000004B6 style:Normal -->
Interaction with Contractors:
 In a meeting hall, Davian meets Tanelle, a young and enthusiastic glyphwright who idolizes the High Clades. Her admiration grates on him, reinforcing his hatred for the system that exploits and misleads people like her.

<!-- paragraph:1207 para_id:000004B7 style:Normal -->
Maya’s Command and an Assassination Attempt:
 Maya Rezin addresses the contractors, explaining the scope of the citadel’s ward overhaul project. As she assigns supervisors, one suddenly attempts to assassinate her. Maya effortlessly dispatches the attacker with her Shroud, freezing and shattering him without emotion, before calmly ordering the room sealed and the project temporarily paused.

<!-- paragraph:1208 para_id:000004B8 style:Normal -->
Davian’s Reflection:
 Witnessing Maya’s cold efficiency and lack of remorse, Davian reflects on how the High Clades see ordinary people as expendable. The moment stokes his anger and resolve, as he vows to make them pay for the pain they’ve caused.

<!-- paragraph:1210 para_id:000004BA style:Normal -->
Chapter 5 outline

<!-- paragraph:1211 para_id:000004BB style:Normal -->
The chapter follows Maya as she navigates her new role as the Rezin heir, practicing with her younger brother Selwin and grappling with the weight of her Presentation and its aftermath. The narrative transitions into a mysterious dream that propels Maya on a secretive journey deep within the Rezin citadel, culminating in the discovery of her mother’s cryptic journal.

<!-- paragraph:1212 para_id:000004BC style:Normal -->
Return to the Citadel
Maya reflects on the tense journey back to the Rezin citadel, Niall’s urgency, and the unspoken consequences of her bold Presentation. Upon arrival, Niall leads her to the secluded training courtyard and explains that her actions will be perceived as a challenge by the other High Clades. He warns her to remain vigilant, especially outside the citadel, as assassins may test her strength.

<!-- paragraph:1213 para_id:000004BD style:Normal -->
Tension with Niall and Training with Selwin
Maya debates Niall’s pragmatic view of lives as “resources” and his belief that emotions lead to weakness, but their argument is interrupted by Selwin’s cheerful arrival. The mood softens as Maya turns her focus to helping Selwin practice basic magical exercises. She reflects on the dangers young High Clade magi face before their abilities fully manifest, using Selwin’s situation to frame the significance of the Presentation.

<!-- paragraph:1214 para_id:000004BE style:Normal -->
Maya’s Dream
That night, Maya experiences a vivid, disorienting dream where she floats through a surreal, shifting space. She sees a woman she believes to be her mother and follows her through the familiar upper corridors of the citadel, which gradually become darker and more ancient. The woman leads her to a glowing alcove deep beneath the citadel, but when Maya touches her shoulder, the figure turns to reveal an inky, faceless void. Maya awakens in terror.

<!-- paragraph:1215 para_id:000004BF style:Normal -->
Journey to the Alcove
Unable to sleep, Maya decides to retrace the path from her dream. She convinces the guards stationed outside her room to stay behind, invoking her authority as the Rezin heir. As she descends into the depths of the citadel, the corridors grow darker and more oppressive. When she reaches the alcove, faint runes illuminate, and she feels a whisper in her mind saying, “I knew you would come.” A stone block moves to reveal a hidden hollow containing a leather-bound journal bearing her mother’s name.

<!-- paragraph:1216 para_id:000004C0 style:Normal -->
Discovery and Unease
Maya takes the journal and notices faint footprints in the dust that aren’t hers. Troubled by their presence, she keeps her Shroud up as she returns to her chambers. The journal is written in an indecipherable cipher, leaving her with more questions than answers. Before going to bed, she resolves to find a way to decrypt the journal, setting the stage for further investigation. Sleep eventually claims her, but the unease of the night lingers.

Oh, also I guess they live in kind of a mini walled manor with Concord members as guards, although it’s a cobbled together dilapidated fortress that was abandoned by a low clade after some internecine conflict or another.

<!-- paragraph:1297 para_id:00000511 style:Heading4 -->
#### IV. Arrival at the Spire

<!-- paragraph:1298 para_id:00000512 style:Normal -->
The spire’s architecture is described in lavish detail, emphasizing its shared ownership by the High Clades and the undercurrent of jealousy and rivalry.

<!-- paragraph:1299 para_id:00000513 style:Normal -->
Maya and Niall are greeted by representatives of the other High Clades, each radiating their distinct magical presence. They’re sitting in front of banners or something

<!-- paragraph:1300 para_id:00000514 style:Normal -->
Quick descriptions of each Clade:

<!-- paragraph:1301 para_id:00000515 style:Normal -->
Archeon (Transcendence): Summoners of spirits, their aura seems ethereal and otherworldly.

<!-- paragraph:1302 para_id:00000516 style:Normal -->
Nyctaris (Nocturne): Wielders of shadow, their presence feels unnerving and cold.

<!-- paragraph:1303 para_id:00000517 style:Normal -->
Drakhal (Aegistry): Radiating strength, their force-magic gives them an imposing aura.

<!-- paragraph:1304 para_id:00000518 style:Normal -->
Cryndor (Severance): Their sharp and deliberate movements reflect their splitting magic.

<!-- paragraph:1305 para_id:00000519 style:Normal -->
Lyranth (Resonance): Their energy seems to ripple outward, as though every movement is amplified.

<!-- paragraph:1306 para_id:0000051A style:Normal -->
Maya exchanges polite but strained greetings with key members of the Clades, particularly focusing on the Drakhal representative (possibly her intended fiancé).

<!-- paragraph:1307 para_id:0000051B style:Heading3 -->
### 4. Erynn’s Observation

<!-- paragraph:1308 para_id:0000051C style:Normal -->
As they move deeper into the Spire, Erynn quietly points out an Archeon envoy whispering to a Cryndor delegate in a shadowed corner. Maya considers the implications of the alliance, reflecting on the constant maneuvering between Clades. Erynn’s observation offers a chance for Maya to show her growing understanding of the subtle intricacies of politics.

<!-- paragraph:1309 para_id:0000051D style:Heading3 -->
### 6. An Awkward Exchange with a Lesser Clade

<!-- paragraph:1310 para_id:0000051E style:Normal -->
A representative of a lesser Clade attempts to ingratiate themselves with Niall, offering veiled flattery and subtle bribes in the form of rare gifts. Niall dismisses them curtly, while Maya notes the desperation in their tone, pondering the stark hierarchy between the High and lesser Clades.

<!-- paragraph:1312 para_id:00000520 style:Normal -->
---

<!-- paragraph:1313 para_id:00000521 style:Heading4 -->
#### V. The Presentation Ceremony

<!-- paragraph:1314 para_id:00000522 style:Normal -->
Maya takes the stage in the grand chamber atop the spire. The room is filled with representatives from all Clades, their collective presence overwhelming.

<!-- paragraph:1315 para_id:00000523 style:Normal -->
Traditional rituals mark her formal induction as a Rezin heir. Her Shroud glows faintly, a reminder of her lineage and power.

<!-- paragraph:1316 para_id:00000524 style:Normal -->
Maya delivers her speech, carefully rehearsed to balance deference to the Clades with a display of her strength and the Rezin family's status.

<!-- paragraph:1317 para_id:00000525 style:Normal -->
Her speech subtly hints at the attack on the fortress, ensuring the Rezins appear unshaken.

<!-- paragraph:1318 para_id:00000526 style:Normal -->
Political dynamics play out in the audience:

<!-- paragraph:1319 para_id:00000527 style:Normal -->
Drakhal members exchange knowing glances, suggesting hidden agendas.

<!-- paragraph:1320 para_id:00000528 style:Normal -->
Archeon representatives radiate an air of detached superiority.

<!-- paragraph:1321 para_id:00000529 style:Normal -->
Nyctaris members watch Maya with unsettling intensity.

<!-- paragraph:1322 para_id:0000052A style:Normal -->
Maya concludes her speech to polite applause, aware of the many eyes scrutinizing her every word and movement.

<!-- paragraph:1328 para_id:00000530 style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:1332 para_id:00000534 style:Normal -->
Maya contemplates the challenges ahead, realizing the Presentation is only the beginning of her journey into the treacherous world of High Clade politics.

<!-- paragraph:1335 para_id:00000537 style:Heading3 -->
### Chapter 2 Summary

<!-- paragraph:1336 para_id:00000538 style:Normal -->
Tension Between Father and Son: Davian and Jalen walk through the quiet city streets after dispersing the Concord members. Jalen notices the severe bruises on Davian's forearms and criticizes his reckless use of magic during the fight against the Low Clade magus. Their conversation reveals lingering pain and resentment, with Davian’s pride and hatred for the Clades clashing with Jalen’s calculated approach to survival.

<!-- paragraph:1337 para_id:00000539 style:Normal -->
Approach to the Syndicate: The duo arrives at the meeting place, an inconspicuous doorway marked by faintly glowing glyphs. They are greeted by a hooded guide who leads them through a maze of ancient, underground corridors. The labyrinth’s age and mysterious construction unnerve Davian, raising questions about its origins.

<!-- paragraph:1338 para_id:0000053A style:Normal -->
Confrontation with the Syndicate: In a dimly lit chamber, Jalen and Davian present the stolen documents to the Syndicate, represented by five hooded figures seated on a dais. The central figure uses an unknown form of magic to examine the documents. The Syndicate reveals their plan to infiltrate the Rezin fortress during its defensive overhaul and demands Jalen assume the identity of an external contractor to steal the Heart.

<!-- paragraph:1339 para_id:0000053B style:Normal -->
Davian’s Declaration: Jalen protests, citing the difficulty of bypassing the Rezin Registry and the impossibility of the task. The Syndicate threatens Jalen’s position, reminding him of their control over the Twilight Concord. Overcome with anger, Davian declares he will take on the mission—not to serve the Syndicate, but to kill Niall Rezin. His outburst intrigues the Syndicate leader, who agrees to help him, laughing gleefully at the added stakes.

<!-- paragraph:1340 para_id:0000053C style:Normal -->
The Ink Boon Ritual: The Syndicate leader initiates the Ink Boon ritual. Dark ink forms an intricate glyph beneath Davian, binding him with tendrils of searing pain. He receives two Boons: the ability to temporarily copy another’s aura (intended for Jalen) and a transformation for Antithesis, allowing it to shift between a sword and a small knife—but only once. The ritual overwhelms Davian, leaving him unconscious.

<!-- paragraph:1341 para_id:0000053D style:Normal -->
Escape Through the Catacombs: Jalen and the guide carry a semi-conscious Davian through the maze-like catacombs. Davian briefly awakens, insisting Jalen leave him behind, but Jalen dismisses the idea, pointing out that the Syndicate wouldn’t waste resources on someone they intended to kill.

<!-- paragraph:1342 para_id:0000053E style:Normal -->
Discovery of Antithesis’ Transformation: After resting at the archway exit, Davian notices the weight of Antithesis is wrong. He discovers it has transformed into a small workman’s knife. Jalen explains the Boon’s limitations: the weapon can only revert to its full size once, so Davian must choose wisely when to transform it.

<!-- paragraph:1343 para_id:0000053F style:Normal -->
Return Home: With Jalen’s support, Davian limps back home, battered but determined. Their bond shows signs of strain yet resilience as they confront the daunting task ahead.

<!-- paragraph:1345 para_id:00000541 style:Normal -->
Chapter 1 Summary:

<!-- paragraph:1346 para_id:00000542 style:Normal -->
Maya’s Return:

<!-- paragraph:1347 para_id:00000543 style:Normal -->
Maya returns to her chambers in a daze, reflecting on the battle. Soldiers acknowledge her with subdued respect, further isolating her as she processes the carnage.

<!-- paragraph:1348 para_id:00000544 style:Normal -->
Erynn expresses concern and gently prods Maya to share what happened. Maya explains the attack and her role in holding the line, downplaying her emotional turmoil.

<!-- paragraph:1349 para_id:00000545 style:Normal -->
Maya and Erynn prepare for the Presentation while discussing intelligence reports, trying to piece together which House orchestrated the assault.

<!-- paragraph:1350 para_id:00000546 style:Normal -->
Niall’s Confrontation with the Wall Commanders:

<!-- paragraph:1351 para_id:00000547 style:Normal -->
Niall summons the wall commanders, Harlun and Enver, demanding an explanation for the breach.

<!-- paragraph:1352 para_id:00000548 style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:1353 para_id:00000549 style:Normal -->
Niall’s Talk with Maya:

<!-- paragraph:1354 para_id:0000054A style:Normal -->
Niall sends Erynn out and confronts Maya about her actions. He points out the recklessness of her first battle experience, emphasizing how dangerous combat is even for seasoned mages.

<!-- paragraph:1355 para_id:0000054B style:Normal -->
He explains that the attack was likely timed to coincide with her Presentation to force the Rezins to reveal her power. Niall notes the strategic significance of her actions but warns against showing vulnerability in such situations.

<!-- paragraph:1356 para_id:0000054C style:Normal -->
Despite his critique, Niall acknowledges her bravery and compares her to her late mother, a rare and poignant moment of praise that leaves Maya conflicted.

<!-- paragraph:1357 para_id:0000054D style:Normal -->
Discovery of Tarran:

<!-- paragraph:1358 para_id:0000054E style:Normal -->
The wall commanders return, reporting they found a surviving soldier too injured to move further. Niall and Maya go to see him in a triage chamber.

<!-- paragraph:1359 para_id:0000054F style:Normal -->
Tarran, burned and maimed from Maya’s fire, defies Niall and refuses to share information, claiming he’s dying.

<!-- paragraph:1360 para_id:00000550 style:Normal -->
Maya intervenes, suggesting healing Tarran so he can speak clearly. Niall agrees reluctantly, sending for a healer.

<!-- paragraph:1361 para_id:00000551 style:Normal -->
The Healer’s Arrival:

<!-- paragraph:1362 para_id:00000552 style:Normal -->
The healer arrives with a rare bonded animal capable of providing near-limitless vitality for magical healing. The creature’s presence underscores the privilege and expense of High Clade resources.

<!-- paragraph:1363 para_id:00000553 style:Normal -->
As Tarran’s wounds begin to mend, Niall halts the process, ensuring Tarran is no longer at risk of dying but still visibly injured. Niall gives him a choice: cooperate and receive full healing or remain crippled.

<!-- paragraph:1364 para_id:00000554 style:Normal -->
Tarran, seeing no alternative, agrees to talk.

<!-- paragraph:1365 para_id:00000555 style:Normal -->
Alden Takes Over:

<!-- paragraph:1366 para_id:00000556 style:Normal -->
Niall summons Alden, the spymaster, who emerges silently from the shadows. Maya is startled by his eerie presence, which seems more like an extension of the room’s darkness than a person.

<!-- paragraph:1367 para_id:00000557 style:Normal -->
Niall instructs Alden to extract information from Tarran and have a report ready by the time they leave for the Presentation.

<!-- paragraph:1368 para_id:00000558 style:Normal -->
Maya follows Niall out, weighed down by the implications of her actions and the looming expectations of the Presentation, questioning whether she’ll ever truly feel at home in this world of calculated power plays.

<!-- paragraph:1371 para_id:0000055B style:Normal -->
The next chapter is from Maya’s POV. Let’s kind of plot it out. She needs to go back to her chambers to keep preparing for Presentation, her maid needs to comment & they kind of discuss what happened. Maya probably feels pretty terrible after blowing a bunch of people up and her dad being weird. Niall comes in later… I’m trying to decide on his exact reaction, like clearly she did the “wrong” thing but he does care about his soldiers and Maya did help them. Maybe he didn’t realize the attack would be so aggressive, he didn’t think the unknown house that attacked would commit so many resources. They do need to think about what house did this, before the council meeting and presentation. Niall needs to talk to Maya about how she needs to be totally devoid of all emotion to control her magic - that shouldn’t quite sit right with her bc of how odd he was during the prologue fight. She could think back about how he changed when her mother died and has been more distant. So all of that, and then they should probably close the chapter on them heading out to the Presentation. Can you give me a little outline and make some suggestions on any additions or changes to make things smoother? Oh one last thing, Niall knows that this attack was probably because Maya’s presentation was that day and someone wanted to force them to reveal their hand so to speak. So they “won” because Maya came out, and Niall killed a lot of their soldiers to try to make them feel it. But he still should be begrudgingly proud that she acted to save their soldiers, while mixing that with fear for her safety that likely subconsciously plays off his feelings for this dead wife.

<!-- paragraph:1373 para_id:0000055D style:Normal -->
So I don’t see how Erynn would know what happened, so Maya should have to tell her what happened. They also should be concretely strategizing about how to figure out who sent the soldiers - they might send someone out to find someone for questioning. They could then find someone who isn’t dead but has their arm burned off from Maya’s fire and is young, and they question him which could give a more human face to the casualties. They should essentially conclude that they know who sent the troops (Drakhal) but they’ll never be able to produce enough evidence to prove it to the council.

Prologue timeline

<!-- paragraph:1382 para_id:00000566 style:Normal -->
We are going to open with a prologue that has a "near miss" event between Davian and Maya. The overall plot is that Davian is infiltrating a Low Clade manor to obtain information for the Syndicate, but the manifest is guarded by the head magus of the Clade so Davian kills him in a duel. While this is happening, the the Rezin fortress is being assaulted by troops from an unknown other Clade. Maya is preparing for her Presentation to the High Clade Council, and Niall is drawn away by the attack. She and her ladies' maid Erynn continue to prepare until soldiers ask them to come help, since they are losing a lot of soldiers. Although it's a bad strategic decision Maya decides to help and uses her magic to destroy many of the attacking soldiers; a beam of fire she uses cuts through the manor where Davian is fighting the Low Clade magus. Eventually Niall comes to finish the fight with Maya, and Davian sees Maya resplendent on the wall of the fortress as he slinks back into the shadows. The scene alternates between their points of view.
