<!-- paragraph:2749 para_id:00000ABD style:Normal -->
Is there a way to make the integration and complexity of the powers be meaningful? Like the idea that every valuable or impactful skill is difficult at first. Swordsmanship involves stance, grip, forms, reading opponents, drilling, body awareness, etc. You’re not going to be an expert right away (although it’s unsatisfying in a fantasy narrative). Davian probably shouldn’t be at the highest level / able to beat Serathis even with her knives at the end of the book. This ties into endgame matchups. Can he beat Brann?

<!-- paragraph:2750 para_id:00000ABE style:Normal -->
It’s not that Davian’s mom was wrong and Harvick is right, it’s that they were giving different views about the same thing, and they’re adapted for different situations. The goal is to be engaged and effective, not just to feel good (although that may be a byproduct)

<!-- paragraph:2751 para_id:00000ABF style:Normal -->
Ask yourself - what purpose is this serving? And if the answer is none, don’t shove it away, but let it pass.

So it’s obvious from the treasury fight Harvick has some… techniques. Remember this was that DBT stuff, like “Codex of the Quiet Flame” (workshop the name). Clearly Davian wasn’t ready for these earlier but if he can turn things around in prison maybe he can… This is a fantasy world, there’s no reason martial skills can’t be super OP

<!-- paragraph:2752 para_id:00000AC0 style:Normal -->
Harvick can teach Davian some specific techniques, but he can’t learn a bunch of them in a short time. If he relies too much on them he’ll become predictable like the Archeon magi. Instead he should focus on his strengths (martial arts plus subversion) and only use the techniques as a backup or to end a fight… or keep them off balance (writing: some of this comes out when he’s learning, but the rest can come out during the final fights)

<!-- paragraph:2753 para_id:00000AC1 style:Normal -->
Now the Black Flash thing from JJK is cool because it’s like a binary thing you can “reach” when you have a certain level of control (balancing too much anger with too little, or harnessing it). What would the equivalent be? Harvick is dumb so he could have been teaching Davian it accidentally

<!-- paragraph:2754 para_id:00000AC2 style:Normal -->
Harvick - you just want to fight everything, all the time… you could try not fighting your thoughts. Yeah maybe you can “win” for a second and fend them off but then they’ll just be back (usually angrier and with more friends)… what if you redirect them, or less them pass you? -when you’re a child, you have less things relying on you and less responsibilities. When you’re an adult, it’s easy to let all those small things build up if you’re not practiced at dealing with them in a way that’s helpful

<!-- paragraph:2755 para_id:00000AC3 style:Normal -->
Harvick forced Davian into fighting so much because he knew he wouldn’t be practicing healthy on his own-Harvick can teach him the “when things get too crazy in your head try mindfulness/meditation” (naming the problem and observing it - could build in projection here but kinda similar to Sanderson) and then he practices doing this more regularly -or it comes back up in this Archeon attack and he remembers that it’s effective, and then it gets drilled more later. You might need to be in this state for the martial arts Harvick knows

Everyone has both healthy and unhealthy coping skills for ex: death anxiety. Just because they work doesn’t mean they’re “right”

- Interruption to kill a spy - They’ve killed several but Serathis knows that means they’ve probably missed at least one and they can’t keep what they’re doing secret forever. The Registry let the Rezins avoid getting their hands dirty by killing spies like every other Clade does, but now they’ll have to let that illusion slip.
- Eventually Serathis sends everyone else out and fights Kelyra herself “Get up, granddaughter. Prove you can earn this.”
- Serathis can break it down for Kelyra. What makes a High Clade a High Clade? Strong enough magic. What is required for strong magic? First, a Shroud. She figured out that Shrouds are a different type of magic, so despite the dogma of “you can’t cross breed to have two types of magic” the exception is you can cross-breed to get a Shroud and another type of magic. Second, you need some kind of hardwired magic circuit for manipulating reality. Third, enough speed of thought and abstract reasoning to use the hardwired magic circuits effectively. Of course, the way these all interact matters - Niall has speed of thought, sure, but he also has the kind of magic that doesn’t require as much cognition per destructive force - he carves down from the sky (or is it up from the ground?) and lets the charge differential do the rest. Half the time he doesn’t even need to carve all the way to his target, since charge will follow the path itself if the person is standing alone. And fourth - training to get those reflexes to be instinctual enough that they can be co-used with other functions, training that starts young. Kelyra didn’t know it, but the Archeon martial arts are specifically designed to help internalize the instincts needed for Shrouds and improve combat abilities. And her breaking out on her own and coming up with some of her own things actually helped because the Archeon magi got stagnant from all learning from the same people (who live a long time) and fighting each other.
She tells Kelyra about how they are “the same” and she will never give up until all the High Clades are destroyed. - no matter how long it takes. -you were always my favorite, daughter. -I’m not really your daughter -how old are you? -another unfortunate casualty of poor clade record keeping. “When he came to me with the gift, I was nothing. He came to you too. That’s what he really wants - equality by destruction of the High Clades, and that’s what you want too.”
- Important point - Kelyra thinks the Harbingers are on the “people’s” side somehow. That’s the lie Elric sells with the Ink Boons - power to the people so the people won’t live in fear (of the high clades). She’s supporting them thinking they are revolutionaries and together with them they can bring the high clades down. And her fantasy - like most revolutionaries - is putting herself at the top, unassailable.

<!-- paragraph:2987 para_id:00000BAB style:Title -->
# Ch32 outline

<!-- paragraph:2988 para_id:00000BAC style:Normal -->
Deeper descent
 Tunnel continues past the alcove, older and more intact. Architecture shifts from Citadel utility to something purpose-built and obsessive. Silence deepens. Niall recognizes the hand of a single architect rather than Clade work.

<!-- paragraph:2989 para_id:00000BAD style:Normal -->
Elric’s workspace revealed
 They enter a chamber that is clearly Elric’s original site:
 – Zan mechanisms embedded directly into stone, not modular, still functioning despite age
 – Zan complexity immediately registers as old and superior; Maya recognizes parallels to Zirene’s work (older logic, denser layering, less symbolic, more structural)
 – Layout suggests long-term habitation and experimentation, not a ritual chamber meant to be abandoned

<!-- paragraph:2990 para_id:00000BAE style:Normal -->
Ink pool
 A contained pool of Ink dominates the space. It is inactive at first but clearly maintained by the zan mechanisms. Niall reacts strongly; Harvick uneasy but curious; Maya senses continuity rather than threat.

<!-- paragraph:2991 para_id:00000BAF style:Normal -->
Triggering the projection
 Interaction with the mechanisms (Maya or Harvick, not Niall) activates the pool. Ink rises and forms a humanoid simulacrum of Elric.
 – Not alive
 – Not hostile
 – An imprint tied to residual aura and prior Ink usage
 – Clearly not expecting them, but able to respond

<!-- paragraph:2992 para_id:00000BB0 style:Normal -->
Failed attack establishes rules
 Niall immediately strikes it with lightning. The blow punches through, then seals. No pain response, no aggression. The projection reacts neutrally or comments on the inefficiency of the attempt. This establishes: it cannot be destroyed by force and is not an enemy in the conventional sense.

<!-- paragraph:2993 para_id:00000BB1 style:Normal -->
Lore via dialogue, not exposition
 They speak with the simulacrum. It answers only within limits, shaped by how questions are asked. Through this:
 – Reality is described as structurally damaged, not morally fallen
 – Elric frames the world as irreparably compromised
 – His tone suggests exhaustion and inevitability
 – Strong implication that he expected or welcomed death, but no confirmation of his end goal
 – No full Harbinger explanation; just philosophical framing and partial technical hints

<!-- paragraph:2994 para_id:00000BB2 style:Normal -->
Niall’s reaction: prohibition reflex
 Niall interprets Elric’s conclusions as proof that fateweaving exposure is corruptive and dangerous. He reiterates that any interaction with fate systems leads to breakdown and must be forbidden.

<!-- paragraph:2995 para_id:00000BB3 style:Normal -->
Maya’s pushback
 Maya counters directly: fateweaving is how she found Davian, how they uncovered this place, how they are even having this conversation. This is not theoretical anymore; banning it would mean choosing blindness.

<!-- paragraph:2996 para_id:00000BB4 style:Normal -->
Ink linkage realization
 Through the simulacrum or the mechanisms, they realize:
 – This Ink pool is tied to the same network Davian was connected to
 – His Ink was not unique or accidental
 – He was plugged into a legacy system, not a rogue mutation

<!-- paragraph:2997 para_id:00000BB5 style:Normal -->
Chapter turn and decision
 They agree the next step is Davian. Not as a prisoner, but as a key. Whatever Elric started, Davian is now part of its continuation whether he wants to be or not.

<!-- paragraph:3027 para_id:00000BD3 style:Normal -->
Davian has been forced to have the “blank slate” style of cognition - lacking the ability to conceptualize others as whole objects as a defense against himself being conceptualized as a whole object (if he is, then why are other people terrible? Why do his parents have issues?) So that leads to initially devaluing Maya and then later idealizing her. When he idealizes her but then has to betray her, that’s where he eventually has to integrate those and see her as a whole person.

<!-- paragraph:3028 para_id:00000BD4 style:Normal -->
Justifying rage or hate or oppression of others (or by others) often involves the defense of painting those people as caricatures. To some extent, that’s what fantasy is about - simplifying abstract issues, or at least making them concrete enough to be hit with a sword. Emotional stability becomes magical strength. Life satisfaction becomes power. They’re things that can be seen and described and affect the external world. When in reality, these affect our internal worlds in just as profound of a way - but that’s not as exciting, is it?

<!-- paragraph:3035 para_id:00000BDB style:Normal -->
Magical effort = difference between energy stored and environment, times the area of the inverted surface, times the average distance of the inverted surface from the magus twice. That’s just a very rough estimate, the shape of the surface and the ability to clearly visualize it at a distance are also important. Effort divided by cognitive speed is strain on the magus. Improving visualization, making shapes more efficient, increasing cognitive speed all reduce the strain on the magus.

Elarion likes to pretend it came up with the advanced jin system, but they really just stole ideas from Naeroth and mass produced them. Naeroth still works with Jin but they focus more on ways to enhance natural features rather than wrest control from the earth. However, they aren’t gullible hippies - they’d recognize that Elarion’s way is just as legitimate and certainly has been helpful for their development. Their techniques would line up exactly with Niall’s needs - advanced, powerful, but designed to be used in moderation for shaping. Niall combines the power and force of Elarion’s Jin development with Naeroth’s techniques and a TON of money to get what he currently has. Archeon did something similar, and that’s also where antithesis comes from - they were looking into swords before they realized gauntlets made more sense, and Kelyra made up the whole “heirloom” thing and stole hers when she left.

<!-- paragraph:3451 para_id:00000D7B style:Normal -->
Board exam metaphor - it’s bursts of intense cognition and focus followed by processing, but the whole time you need to be at least moderately activated. <!-- paragraph:3452 para_id:00000D7C style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:3456 para_id:00000D80 style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:3457 para_id:00000D81 style:Normal -->
⁃	what I’m saying is there are a lot of heuristic assumptions about how things work based on how they feel

<!-- paragraph:3458 para_id:00000D82 style:Normal -->
⁃	Elric did an experiment based on precisely attacking multiple objects simultaneously. If they were stationary or moved in a predictable pattern, it was possible for the mind to simplify it in such a way that it was possible. But if the patterns became unpredictable, no one but Niall could even track two at a time. And Niall noted that he could feel a clear, rapid switching of attention between the objects. That was back when Cryndor and Drakhal were friendly enough to participate in Elric’s experiments. It’s possible they faked their abilities being worse than they were, but that would have been against their pride and generally it pays better to fake that you’re stronger than weaker.

<!-- paragraph:3459 para_id:00000D83 style:Normal -->
⁃	The point is - we don’t even know how our own minds work. We just hear explanations that make sense and teach them, pass them down - but just because the explanation is elegant and makes sense doesn’t mean it’s right. <!-- paragraph:3593 para_id:00000E09 style:Normal -->
Magic (hereditary) requires a literally inhuman level of control - part of what was baked into the magi’s genetics is this rapid processing split focus that allows them to use the magic at all. But, that has psychological consequences.

<!-- paragraph:3595 para_id:00000E0B style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:3599 para_id:00000E0F style:Normal -->
Subversion and shrouds are similar manifestations of primordial magic - the shroud is the non-reality-distortion one and subversion is the reality distorting version of the same thing. The shroud relies on the underlying hereditary magic to absorb the sublimated (subverted?) energy. Subversion does have backlash but it’s disproportionately small to the energy being transformed - if the magic is used efficiently. That means using it smartly as an overlay on a shroud can allow the sublimation to be very subtle, reducing the strength of magic needed for a powerful shroud.

<!-- paragraph:3601 para_id:00000E11 style:Normal -->
Remember backlash - a proficient magus will channel any backlash energy into their shroud to be sublimated, but that takes additional cognitive effort

<!-- paragraph:3611 para_id:00000E1B style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:3612 para_id:00000E1C style:Normal -->
9) Cognitive/physiology primer during setup: Harvick notes Shroud is “background” like balance—pretrained, reflexive loops; as magi age, pros: ingrained pathways; cons: reduced flexibility/switching; magi do cardio for cognition/endurance, rarely heavy strength (not needed if Shroud converts energy); “we call it splitting focus but it’s switching + holding structures”—elegant lies taught as truths.

<!-- paragraph:3613 para_id:00000E1D style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:3617 para_id:00000E21 style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:3618 para_id:00000E22 style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:3619 para_id:00000E23 style:Normal -->

No guaranteed win; deterrence + erosion: others resist via delay/incompetence just short of provoking him; pride prevented public admission they were cowed, so “spontaneous cooperation” myth persisted; blame-shifting after attacks (“we only matched Niall’s terror”); Niall can’t be punished; things decay at the margins.

 Maya joins Davian’s table; warmth of group vs cold status; Davian honest, treats her as person; ink boon aura a touch faded since fight → Maya (light tease) asks about tattoos/$$; Davian deflects: common, traditional—she’d know if she left the Citadel; micro-misstep: she mentions the Registry catching him going into the city → he reads it as surveillance; they clock each other’s states: “you’re stressed” / “there’s a dark look in your eyes”; Selwin may drop in—unconditional positive regard, gentle mirror for both; other jinwrights give Davian looks (gossip fuel).

<!-- paragraph:3629 para_id:00000E2D style:Normal -->
//S3 Harvick interrupts → pivots to “hands-on research”
 Harvick flags Archeon predictability; invites Maya (and Davian, Erynn, possibly Selwin): co-op study session now; frame: shroud/martial overlays; aim: practical tests not library only; Maya wants face time; Davian conflicted but goes (Harvick thinks they’re good for each other).

<!-- paragraph:3630 para_id:00000E2E style:Normal -->
//S4 field lab: shroud–martial integration tests
 Site: training yard/workshop; gear: gauntlets (inside shroud), glyph lattices/batteries; drills: body-as-focus → faster channeling; redirect energy (Subversion overlay) into shroud to sublimate backlash; show that kinetic conversion via shroud + Subversion timing spikes strength; cardio matters for cognition; older magi: more ingrained pathways, less flexibility; things impossible to calculate in real time become doable when pre-trained heuristics/forms; shroud runs “background” like balance; Maya logs: constant awareness shaping localized reality.

<!-- paragraph:3631 para_id:00000E2F style:Normal -->
//S5 Archeon hypothesis (group dialogue; Harvick lead, Maya observed it)
 Archeon drills a handful of synchronized moves (jump/kick/punch variants) executed with shroud+Subversion → very high temporary power; can’t adapt on the fly → bum-rush, kill fast (mono-red metaphor); predictability seen in attack; compounded by form-memorization culture in shroud arts; political mask: sold as “super shroud/genetic superiority” → high clades accepted narrative; Drakhal knows truth, not threatened.

<!-- paragraph:3632 para_id:00000E30 style:Normal -->
//S6 cognition focus mythbust (Elric experiment recap)
 “Splitting focus” is switching speed + holding structures; Elric tested simultaneous precise attacks: works only for stationary/predictable targets; with unpredictability, only Niall tracked two (rapid attention switching felt); Cryndor/Drakhal cooperated then (pride likely prevented sandbagging); elegant explanations ≠ truth—magi still repeat myths; takeaway for Archeon: make targets unpredictable faster than their switching; link to Maya’s worry about premeditated killing vs reflex.

<!-- paragraph:3633 para_id:00000E31 style:Normal -->
//S7 shroud vs hereditary magic (physics poke)
 Current dogma: shrouds “sublimate” incoming energy into your heredity; contradiction: hereditary magic breaks/redirects natural law, so how do shrouds transform energy form? → suggests shroud is a separate primordial modality; Subversion + Shroud = same family (non-distorting vs distorting); efficient Subversion overlay can let weaker heredity ride a strong shroud; backlash can be routed into shroud but costs cognition; Naeroth logs might show “when did that change?”; Niall’s lightning visual is top-down but energy may source from ground (map ≠ territory).

<!-- paragraph:3634 para_id:00000E32 style:Normal -->
//S8 values + vulnerability micro-beats (bonding tissue)
 Short exchange on true values: who do you want to be (for you)?; Maya admits body-as-focus helps channel; Davian admits attraction to her stability; Maya opens maskless moment; Davian signals “still like you” without making it grand; both share core value: protect the innocent; Maya processes being seen → forces identity beyond symbol.

<!-- paragraph:3635 para_id:00000E33 style:Normal -->
//S9 fallout/aftermath threads (politics + Niall context)
 Registry was drained by Caius earlier; other magi will blame Niall/Maya for excesses (cover story after losses); Niall can’t be punished, so resistance = delay/incompetence; system demands inhuman perfection or brutality; Niall’s depression → apathy; reason he doesn’t rush Archeon/Drakhal: no guaranteed win; Delta Green sanity vibe: knowing warps you (Elric, Maya; threads talk awkward near Niall).

<!-- paragraph:3636 para_id:00000E34 style:Normal -->
//S10 Selwin check-in (optional button within session or walk-back)
 Selwin’s Dissolution aftermath; psychological state raw; brief Davian–Selwin beat: Davian sees himself in Selwin → empathy lens on Maya; keeps Selwin in orbit for later training thread.

<!-- paragraph:3637 para_id:00000E35 style:Normal -->
//S11 closing beat (Maya takeaways -> next actions)
 Maya synthesizes: Archeon predictable via precomputed forms; plan: design unpredictable drills; pursue Naeroth “before/after” logs; test mixed gauntlet protocols; consider shroud-as-separate-magic; share selective insights with Davian (danger: later theft); choice: warmth of friendship over isolated status; internal note: perfectionism “shoulds” vs values choice.

<!-- paragraph:3638 para_id:00000E36 style:Normal -->

# Ch24 extra notes

<!-- paragraph:3646 para_id:00000E3E style:Heading2 -->
## 2) Summons from “mother” (letter) interrupts

<!-- paragraph:3647 para_id:00000E3F style:Normal -->
Delivery: A runner hands Davian (as Arrek) a folded note sealed with a small, generic mark used by the Veiled/underclass (or a known sign agreed on with his mother).

<!-- paragraph:3648 para_id:00000E40 style:Normal -->
Content: “Come.” Sparse, code-short. (We keep phrasing deliberately minimal; it’s a private channel.)

<!-- paragraph:3649 para_id:00000E41 style:Normal -->
Davian beat: He knows he’s lying to her by continuing this cover, but he wants to pretend a little longer, selfishly—especially because the thought of Maya scrambled his certainties.

<!-- paragraph:3650 para_id:00000E42 style:Normal -->
Placement: Arrives right as he feels marginally good about getting through the morning without spiraling (so it punctures the high).

<!-- paragraph:3651 para_id:00000E43 style:Normal -->
It’s a bill for something - but he knows what it’s really a bill for

<!-- paragraph:3654 para_id:00000E46 style:Normal -->
Harvick response (core lesson):

<!-- paragraph:3655 para_id:00000E47 style:Normal -->
Acceptance ≠ liking or forgiving. It’s letting reality be real so you can act with both eyes open.

<!-- paragraph:3656 para_id:00000E48 style:Normal -->
Humans (and the underclass) still decide everything around the magi: supply lines, evacuations, protecting civilians, and the moments before a magus arrives. That window matters.

<!-- paragraph:3657 para_id:00000E49 style:Normal -->
Subtext confession seed: Harvick uses training as exposure for himself; he once killed a young man (regret). He does this to stay on the Brine, not the Void.

<!-- paragraph:3658 para_id:00000E4A style:Normal -->
Davian retort: “So we just accept living under people who can erase us by blinking?”

<!-- paragraph:3659 para_id:00000E4B style:Normal -->
Harvick: “You accept that they can—and then you train to move before the blink.”

<!-- paragraph:3660 para_id:00000E4C style:Normal -->
---

<!-- paragraph:3661 para_id:00000E4D style:Heading2 -->
## 5) Maya context drop (Harvick advocates for her; “she has no one”)

<!-- paragraph:3662 para_id:00000E4E style:Normal -->
Harvick lays out her isolation: People are trying to kill her; everything she does has political blowback; Erynn is dear but shares none of Maya’s burden; her father & brother are unstable/dangerous in different ways.

<!-- paragraph:3663 para_id:00000E4F style:Normal -->
Point: Davian and Maya share a core value—protecting the innocent—even if they come from opposite worlds.

<!-- paragraph:3664 para_id:00000E50 style:Normal -->
Davian bristles: Claims he doesn’t respect her “status,” only reacts to a person. (Good—Harvick marks that as real honesty breaking through Davian’s masks.)

<!-- paragraph:3665 para_id:00000E51 style:Normal -->
---

<!-- paragraph:3666 para_id:00000E52 style:Heading2 -->
## 8) Training scene #1 (courtyard mat / private salle) — trust vs. Shroud

<!-- paragraph:3667 para_id:00000E53 style:Normal -->
Setup: Harvick “refs,” then steps back. Maya arrives slightly injured (strains/singe; bandage under sleeve), insists defenses matter more than ever; no time to pause.

<!-- paragraph:3668 para_id:00000E54 style:Normal -->
Davian objection: “I can’t do anything to you with that Shroud up.”

<!-- paragraph:3669 para_id:00000E55 style:Normal -->
Harvick (dry): “You’ll have to trust him not to hurt you.” (little revenge for Davian’s earlier attitude)

<!-- paragraph:3670 para_id:00000E56 style:Normal -->
Maya decision: Drops the Shroud to skin-level (thin film, not zero), cold breath frosting the air; she’s in control but vulnerable.

<!-- paragraph:3671 para_id:00000E57 style:Normal -->
Instruction beats (experiential):

<!-- paragraph:3672 para_id:00000E58 style:Normal -->
Breath + stance (Naeroth-adjacent) — “Your mind is the loom your magic is woven on.” (Erynn will later quote this from Maya’s books; here we seed the line as training lore.)

<!-- paragraph:3673 para_id:00000E59 style:Normal -->
Close-in entries → how to interrupt a stronger opponent’s structure (hips/shoulder line) without trading blows; wrist control to redirect energy (mirrors Subversion principles).

<!-- paragraph:3674 para_id:00000E5A style:Normal -->
Maya slips a truth about magic: the shortest channel (body as focus) reduces cognitive distance and accelerates Convergence. (Davian notes this—and, yes, notes her body in proximity, cue attraction spike/guilt.)

<!-- paragraph:3675 para_id:00000E5B style:Normal -->
Micro-move: She executes a simple entry → inside foot hook → shoulder turn. Davian yields, surprised. He likes teaching her and hates that he likes it.

<!-- paragraph:3678 para_id:00000E5E style:Heading3 -->
### A Realistic Option: Leg Sweep + Slam

<!-- paragraph:3679 para_id:00000E5F style:Normal -->
One of the simplest ways to knock someone flat:

<!-- paragraph:3680 para_id:00000E60 style:Normal -->
Set-up

<!-- paragraph:3681 para_id:00000E61 style:Normal -->
Opponent squares off. Maya steps in close rather than backing away (Davian would emphasize that retreat isn’t always an option).

<!-- paragraph:3682 para_id:00000E62 style:Normal -->
She uses one arm to control or push the upper body (for Vorren this could be a shove to the chest/shoulder or pulling on his clothing/armor).

<!-- paragraph:3683 para_id:00000E63 style:Normal -->
The Sweep

<!-- paragraph:3684 para_id:00000E64 style:Normal -->
At the same moment, she uses her leg to hook behind his ankle/calf (often called a foot sweep in Judo/Krav Maga).

<!-- paragraph:3685 para_id:00000E65 style:Normal -->
Driving force comes from the push or pull up top combined with sweeping the leg out from under him.

<!-- paragraph:3686 para_id:00000E66 style:Normal -->
Done hard, it takes balance completely away — even a much bigger opponent goes down because gravity does the work.

<!-- paragraph:3687 para_id:00000E67 style:Normal -->
The Slam

<!-- paragraph:3688 para_id:00000E68 style:Normal -->
Instead of just letting him fall, she drives him down by following through with her weight.

<!-- paragraph:3689 para_id:00000E69 style:Normal -->
That could mean keeping her grip on his arm/shoulder and riding him to the ground, so it reads less like a gentle sweep and more like she rips him onto his back.

<!-- paragraph:3691 para_id:00000E6B style:Normal -->
---

<!-- paragraph:3692 para_id:00000E6C style:Heading2 -->
## 9) Class tension: tattoos & the Shade

<!-- paragraph:3693 para_id:00000E6D style:Normal -->
Maya (studying him up close): Mentions she saw the Shade’s tattoos; asks how much coin he wastes on ink.

<!-- paragraph:3694 para_id:00000E6E style:Normal -->
Davian (even): “A lot of people have these. They’re traditional. You’d know that if you ever left the citadel.”

<!-- paragraph:3695 para_id:00000E6F style:Normal -->
Subtext: she flinches; he instantly regrets the sting; she absorbs it without lashing out (perfectionist mask), files it under I don’t know the city I rule.

<!-- paragraph:3696 para_id:00000E70 style:Normal -->
---

<!-- paragraph:3697 para_id:00000E71 style:Heading2 -->
## 10) Argument spike → core-value alignment

<!-- paragraph:3698 para_id:00000E72 style:Normal -->
Maya (compressed shame/anger): “They hate me. For something I can’t control. I can control everything else—work, speed, precision—but not this.”

<!-- paragraph:3699 para_id:00000E73 style:Normal -->
(Her speed is the outward manifestation of perfectionism: If I’m fast enough, I can stay in control.)

<!-- paragraph:3700 para_id:00000E74 style:Normal -->
Davian counters (and reveals himself): “They hate you because you tried to do something good. If you do the right thing, some people will hate you. You told the High Clades what they needed to hear—not what kept them comfortable. That reaction is on them.”

<!-- paragraph:3701 para_id:00000E75 style:Normal -->
(Mind the earlier Aldira line; keep this punchier, rougher, less mentorly.)

<!-- paragraph:3702 para_id:00000E76 style:Normal -->
Maya escalates: “And now I have to kill them.”

<!-- paragraph:3703 para_id:00000E77 style:Normal -->
Davian snaps: “There it is again—‘we’re all evil.’ You can’t define yourself by what you hate.”

<!-- paragraph:3704 para_id:00000E78 style:Normal -->
He hears his own hypocrisy mid-sentence; the Boon whispers push emptiness-if-no-hate. His jaw locks. Harvick clocks the crack.

<!-- paragraph:3705 para_id:00000E79 style:Normal -->
---

<!-- paragraph:3706 para_id:00000E7A style:Heading2 -->
## 11) Training scene #2 (application pass) — unexpected success

<!-- paragraph:3707 para_id:00000E7B style:Normal -->
Harvick, brisk: “Again.”

<!-- paragraph:3708 para_id:00000E7C style:Normal -->
Drill: Close-quarters entanglement, then a surprise beat—Maya uses the taught entry plus a Naeroth breath cue to break posture and check Davian’s arm cleanly. Davian yields, genuinely impressed.

<!-- paragraph:3709 para_id:00000E7D style:Normal -->
Foreshadow: Harvick aside to Maya (or a look to Davian) that this exact mechanic can end a “punchy” opponent fast. (Set the seed for a later encounter where she drops a non-magus with it.)

<!-- paragraph:3710 para_id:00000E7E style:Normal -->
Davian high: For a breath he feels good—the shared values, the learning, the closeness.

<!-- paragraph:3711 para_id:00000E7F style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:3712 para_id:00000E80 style:Heading2 -->
## 12) Boon backlash + fate-glimmer

<!-- paragraph:3713 para_id:00000E81 style:Normal -->
Boon flare: The dark threads tug; the “evil eyes” sensation returns; his pupils halo; a faint ink sheen at forearm seams. He shakes it off.

<!-- paragraph:3714 para_id:00000E82 style:Normal -->
Maya POV leak (diegetic within Davian chapter): She notices a fate-thread shimmer around him for a heartbeat (she can’t name it; just that threads tilt near him). She files it without comment. (This forwards “Elric is opening Davian up” consequence.)

<!-- paragraph:3715 para_id:00000E83 style:Normal -->
Davian covers: Cracks a joke, returns to stance; Harvick studies his forearms, concerned.

<!-- paragraph:3716 para_id:00000E84 style:Normal -->

<!-- paragraph:3717 para_id:00000E85 style:Heading2 -->
## 13) Harvick calls the self-sabotage

<!-- paragraph:3718 para_id:00000E86 style:Normal -->
Harvick (quiet, direct): “You act like the worst is inevitable so you can behave in ways that make it inevitable. It saves you from hope. That’s Void talking.”

<!-- paragraph:3719 para_id:00000E87 style:Normal -->
Davian bristles, says nothing. The words land.

<!-- paragraph:3720 para_id:00000E88 style:Normal -->
---

<!-- paragraph:3721 para_id:00000E89 style:Heading2 -->
## 14) Chapter turn — the letter’s hook closes; stakes reminder

<!-- paragraph:3722 para_id:00000E8A style:Normal -->
Runner returns (or he re-reads the earlier note): mother expects him tonight.

<!-- paragraph:3723 para_id:00000E8B style:Normal -->
Internal: Everything he’s building with Maya—and with Harvick—is built on a lie with an expiration date. He repeats the mission to himself (treasury, Heart, Concord), clings to rage so the humiliation and tenderness don’t swallow him.

<!-- paragraph:3724 para_id:00000E8C style:Normal -->
Final exchange with Maya (low, charged):

<!-- paragraph:3725 para_id:00000E8D style:Normal -->
She thanks him professionally; reasserts duty: “Our defenses matter more than ever.” She moves fast—too fast—again.

<!-- paragraph:3726 para_id:00000E8E style:Normal -->
He almost says “Be careful.” Instead: “Don’t rush the loom.” (Calls back the line; it lands.) “I am the loom.”

<!-- paragraph:3727 para_id:00000E8F style:Normal -->
Hard exit image: Davian watches her cross the courtyard, speed like a blade. The Boon whispers: Empty without hate. He chooses the wrong thing: go to the meeting anyway.

<!-- paragraph:3728 para_id:00000E90 style:Normal -->
Chapter button: He turns toward the lower city and the rendezvous, knowing he’ll keep pretending a little longer.

<!-- paragraph:3729 para_id:00000E91 style:Normal -->
Inner conflict: He lies cleanly; admits to himself he’s doing it because the lie lets him have both (mission + the feeling of belonging he’s tasting with Maya/Harvick).
